Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

"Making Heroes Lose Heart" 208

— Zi Nan

The Ping Social Affairs Bureau has banned the performances of "Fengbo Pavilion" and "Walking to Maicheng", the crime being that they "make heroes lose heart."

I lack a lot of knowledge about Peking opera, but I have seen both of these plays. Probably because I am not a "hero," I did not "lose heart." On the contrary, I respected and loved Guan Yu and Yue Fei even more: they really seemed like "heroes," unyielding until death.

The perspective of Peking opera is not very correct, that is the truth. But its shortcoming is not "making heroes lose heart," but rather feudal advocacy of blind loyalty and filial piety, as well as things like "chastity" and "martyrdom." Even if there are plays that "make heroes lose heart," it is definitely not "Fengbo Pavilion" or "Walking to Maicheng."

The stories of "Fengbo Pavilion" and "Walking to Maicheng" are generally known to most people, so there is no need to talk about them here. Although the causes of death of these two "heroes" are different—one died in resistance to the enemy and was killed unyieldingly, and the other was framed by a traitor and thus could not "drink to victory at Huanglong"—the admiration I, an ordinary person, have for these two "heroes" is the same. When we criticize Guan Yu and Yue Fei from the perspective of the modern era, there are certainly things that can be criticized. However, I absolutely believe in the saying "Generals should die on the battlefield, not in bed." Measuring Guan Yu and Yue Fei with this concept, I feel that Guan Yu and Yue Fei do not fail the word "hero."

As for saying that after watching "Walking to Maicheng" and "Fengbo Pavilion," it will "make heroes lose heart," this is probably the view of "modern heroes." As someone who is not a "hero," I only feel that Guan Yu and Yue Fei died as they should. If a "hero" unfortunately encounters such a situation, then such a death is truly what is called "heavier than Mount Tai." Of course, it is better to be able to avoid such misfortune and be able to live more meaningfully, but if you encounter it, it is also "glorious" and not "losing heart" in any way.

Not long ago, an old lady named Xiao in the north celebrated her birthday, and the performance was said to be very lively. Almost all of the top actors in the country were there. Recently, it is said that the 29th Army also specially invited the Fu Liancheng class. These two performances were both before the Ping Social Affairs Bureau explicitly prohibited them. I don't know if "Fengbo Pavilion" and "Walking to Maicheng" were included in the program? But based on conjecture, since those two plays "make heroes lose heart," they would probably be avoided. But what plays that "shouldn't make heroes lose heart" are performed? That is probably specially performing "sentimental stories" such as "Little Shepherd Boy" and "Baochan Delivering Wine"? Those plays are neither offensive nor quite in line with the way of "entertainment." Or, thinking that there are too few humorous plays, which, from a "hero's" perspective, lack dignity, then perhaps some elegant and suave "Meilong Town" or "Red-Haired Horse" are performed. These plays are not only elegant and suave, but also have the authority of "being the big brother." With a successful start and instant success, wouldn't that be the ultimate in "enhancing one's own prestige"?

After Seeing "Motherland" 209

— Li Yi

China Traveling Theater Performs at Carlton

The "China Traveling Theater," which has been away from us for three months, has now returned to Shanghai. This time, in addition to keeping "Thunderstorm," other meaningless so-called "technical samples" will reportedly be abandoned. In the current situation of national crisis and deepening national disaster, such a resolute decision is what every conscientious artist should have. And "Motherland," translated and directed by Mr. Chen Mian, is the first play in this new starting point. (I hope this observation is not wrong, in other words, the "China Traveling Theater" is "burying everything from the past to unfold a new future.")

Page 20

Strictly speaking, "Motherland" certainly has many debatable points, but if we make a vertical observation of the "China Traveling Theater," then I dare say; "Motherland" is one of the most meaningful plays performed by the "China Traveling Theater." To borrow a phrase from Mr. Tang Jiqiu, "Motherland" is the closest to "not leaving the era, not leaving the big wind" among the plays of the "China Traveling Theater."

Naturally, precisely because it is meaningful, in addition to expressing our admiration, we will more strictly examine the weaknesses in "Motherland."

First of all, what I want to discuss with Mr. Chen Mian is the aspect of scene division. Based on my shallow experience, among the dramas I have seen, "Motherland" has the most number of acts, because the number of acts is large, the scenery, costumes, props, etc. cannot but be numerous, which is an obvious fact, and this does not seem very suitable for the Chinese theater industry, which is still economically weak. Secondly, because the background of each act is different, the disassembly and installation of each act takes a lot of time, which seems too uneconomical in terms of time. Taking this trial performance as an example, it took almost five hours from the opening to the closing. The staff on stage must be very tired, not to mention the fact that the audience also feels that the play is too long.

As for "Motherland" itself, I feel that several scenes can be deleted, such as the "Outside the City" in the third act, and the "Street" in the seventh act. It is not difficult to explain it clearly simply by adding a few lines in another act. And the second act, if it is properly merged with another act, I think it is not difficult to delete it, right? And the scenery like the third and seventh acts, let alone the fact that it is not easy to please.

I don't think it is a bad thing to modify a good play in order to get rid of the inessential and preserve the essence.

The country of Flanders in "Motherland" is very similar to our current "Motherland." The audience is moved by the patriotism of the patriots on stage, and then looks back at ourselves, so we can't bear to leave immediately. I think this is the most real reason why the audience doesn't "draw lots" [to leave early], but we can't just be satisfied with this. At the same time, I believe that if we modify it properly to make "Motherland" more compact, its power will be even greater. During the trial performance, the general audience was composed of highly educated intellectuals, who of course understand drama better than the average audience. Therefore, in order to consider the general audience, we should take into account their level of appreciation. After a very long time, if a scene suddenly relaxes, what kind of effect will this have? This really makes me "worry about the sky falling." I think the reason why "Thunderstorm" is a box office success and why the audience does not leave even though it takes more than four hours to perform is due to the tight writing.

Moreover, the performance of "Motherland" is only the new starting point of the "China Traveling Theater." If the box office is not very good because of the lack of form, this will make some people use it as an excellent piece of evidence to argue that "conscious plays" (there is such a strange term in the market) do not make money, and, in terms of the "China Traveling Theater's" finances, such a thing is of course undesirable.

A good play should not only have good content, but also a good form to coordinate with it in a unified way: the reason why some plays with very good content in the past did not sell well, allowing certain people to insult them at will, is precisely because of this.

As for the content of Motherland, generally speaking, it can be said to be very good. However, looking down on the enemy too much, thinking that they are all fools, will cause the audience to have a mentality of underestimating the enemy. In fact, the enemy is not only not confused, but may even be more shrewd than us. And the release of a patriot actually owes its blessing to the merciful daughter of the enemy marshal, and the marshal is actually unable to resist his daughter. This is an overly beautiful ideal.

There is a lot to say about directing, and the length of this article does not allow me to talk more about it, so I will omit it and wait for another opportunity to talk about it later. Next, I would like to say a few simple words about other aspects.

Stage setting and lighting were originally the strengths of the "China Traveling Theater," and this is not bad here either, except for the fact that the outdoor scene in the second act and the street in the seventh act are fundamentally difficult to please. Especially in the first act, the lighting makes people feel very good, but in the eighth act, there should have been some light outside the window first, and then it should have turned red, which would definitely make the audience feel more realistic and reduce the sudden feeling.

Probably because it was a preview, the actors' lines and movements were a bit stiff.

Tang Ruoqing's voice is much better than before. If she can pay more attention to her lines, her performance will definitely be more than this. Among all the actors in "Motherland", she is the best actress.

In short, this is the best play among the existing plays of the "China Traveling Theater." I dare to introduce it to you like this.

Mute 210

— Li Xuan

"Dad, it's terrible, there's a 'fallen one' (sick corpse) in our sorghum field."

The old man suddenly threw the hoe to the ground, turning his two lifeless fish eyes.

"What, let's go, go, go, damn it... you're the one who finds trouble."

"How am I, what if they die, then wouldn't that..."

"Don't say such unlucky things, if they die, I'll make you pay with your life!"

When the father and son angrily walked there, the naked person had already climbed into the bean sprouts to hide. The two of them stooped and walked in. The man was crawling under the lush green leaves, picking a handful of tender bean pods to eat. The old man's heart ached even more urgently. He walked over and kicked him, scolding:

"You troublemaker, get out of here!"

The man whimpered like a duck, pointed his finger at his mouth, and waved his hand. "Who's buying livestock with you? You're still using hand gestures!" The old man scolded angrily and was about to kick again when his son stopped him with his hand, saying:

"He's a mute, it's no use getting angry with him."

"Come on! Drag him out!"

The two men grabbed one arm each, and the mute cried out, shaking his head and trying to crawl without moving. The old man stared angrily, pained by the crushed bean sprouts. He also hated why this debtor only chose his field. He snorted, stepped over the mute, and like riding a horse, stretched his hands directly under the man's armpits, and lifted him up violently. The mute howled like a wolf and knelt down. The young man was stunned. When he saw the mute's sagging breasts, he cried out:

"Dad, don't move, it's a woman!"

The old man also sighed in dismay and drew back, feeling unlucky.

The two squatted down at the same time, looking annoyed at the woman lying in the dirt. At this time, someone on the path on the riverbank called:

"Little Pi, Little Pi, I've brought the food!"

The young man responded loudly. The old woman, hanging a large willow basket, walked over following the sound. She looked in surprise at her husband with his bristly beard, and stared straight at her son in the bean leaves. She put down the basket and moved a small pot of porridge down as well. There was a rustling sound in the bean sprouts, then a fluffy head popped out again, whimpering. The old woman said, not daring to move in shock:

"What's going on?"

"A naked mute woman, what do you think we should do?"

As soon as the old woman walked in front of the mute, she whimpered again, grabbed the old woman's trouser legs, and dragged her down with all her might. The two struggled with each other until the old man went to pull his wife back.

The old woman calmed down and said:

"She's naked, she's afraid of seeing men." The old farmer narrowed his eyes and glanced at the bean leaves:

"Who has pants for her to wear!"

"If we ask the head of the village to send her away, and the village chief finds out, won't we have to spend more money?"

The old man handed the old patched blue cloth jacket from his shoulder to his wife and said, "Wrap it around her and send her to the woods in the Ma family's forest." Turning back, he ordered his son to carry the food basket, and he himself held the porridge pot, walked through the rustling sorghum stalks, and walked into the cornfield, turning his head and shouting:

"Send her over there, and bring back the jacket! What a curse..."

School Opening 211

— Shen Jiaqian

The owner of the Hongxing Opium and Cigarette Shop refused a customer who wanted to buy ×× brand cigarettes, "A woman knows nothing," slipped lightly from his throat. ×× brand cigarettes are quite popular in the market now, and many customers come to Hongxing Opium and Cigarette Shop every day to buy this brand. But the owner saw only a few basic cigarettes lying quietly in the cabinet and hit his own palm with his fist, grumbling at his old wife, "A woman knows nothing, ignoring good business and hiding the money to pay for your gold coffin and silver casket."

The Hongxing Opium and Cigarette Shop is located on a small, not-so-busy street. The shop's business still relies on Suzhou and Guangdong general merchandise. The proprietress is a shrewd woman and naturally unwilling to buy expensive ×× brand cigarettes to cater to the few customers. As soon as the owner grumbled, the proprietress immediately jumped up: "At this age, you still don't know how to do business. How many people can afford ×× brand! Kerosene is going to increase in price, and you still don't know to buy a few boxes to store away early."

The owner was henpecked. Although he was unhappy about turning away business, what was the point of buying more kerosene when there were already three large boxes in the shop? He glared at his wife, considering it a moral victory, and walked out of the counter. While the couple was bickering, a letter was dropped on the floor of the shop. The owner picked it up and, after seeing the three characters "Liu Caifu" clearly written on it, found another topic: "The semester is coming again. If you don't do more business, how do you expect to spend during the festival?" He shouted loudly to his son, " Fusheng, come and see what's written in this letter!"

The owner pulled out the letter, but besides the three characters "Liu Caifu," he couldn't recognize anything else.

Fusheng walked out of the inner room of the shop. He was used to the bickering of the old couple, and every resolution ended with Fusheng being dragged in and scolded. He stood blankly in front of his father, took the letter, and glanced sideways at his mother's face.

"School is about to start. It's a notice from the school."

"See!" The owner grabbed another topic: "It's asking for money again, asking for money again!"

The proprietress was calculating, figuring out whether it was worthwhile to buy a few boxes of kerosene. But the proprietress's abacus skills were not very good; the thirteen rods of the abacus seemed not enough for her to manage. She was trying to remember how many days the three boxes of kerosene she had in stock could last, while calculating on the abacus how much interest the capital for buying kerosene could generate. The owner's constant demands for money confused the numbers in her head and on the abacus, so she slammed the abacus down and rushed towards the owner (To be continued)

Storytelling 215

Cao Xiaoying's Yu Qing Ting (Jade Dragonfly)

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Granny Gan's Evening Makeup"

The pond water rises, mooring fishing boats. Drooping willows, ten thousand strands. At dawn, one hears the sound of rowing awakening dreams. The pretty fisherwoman hurriedly throws off the quilt. She is thin and reluctant to get up. She is sleepy-eyed and afraid to look closely. She is too lazy to stretch her lotus-like arms while yawning. She is neatly fastening her cloth garment around her slender waist. One sees her propping a bamboo pole against the copper basin by the window. One sees her picking up clothes and adding a half-sleeve. One sees her lightly opening the mirror case and painting her eyebrows. And one sees her smoothing her hair with a sprig of spring cloud, twisting her hair into a snake-like style. Opening the powder box, she gathers her hands. She lightly applies rouge to her cherry lips, reflecting in the water, startling the shadow of a wild goose. And she carefully draws her eyebrows with willow charcoal. Words cannot describe her graceful demeanor and charming appearance. A single glance is enough to captivate one's soul. The fisherwoman finishes her makeup, puts away the case, and beckons to the net-weaving boat. Suddenly, one hears the light sound of oars.

Dunben (800) 9:05 PM to 10:00 PM

Opening "Chai Tou Feng" (Phoenix Hairpin)

Sentimentality is, in fact, a form of infatuation. Beautiful women with tragic fates have existed since ancient times. I, Zhuanxian, lost my parents at a young age and had no one to rely on. I, alone, am raised as a daughter-in-law in the Lu family. The aunt arranged the marriage out of righteousness. The family happily lived together but then disaster came. I regret not having kindly advised her to avoid creating enmity. The Phoenix Hairpin was shattered unintentionally. This unexpected misfortune was not light. Stirring up trouble was merely to seek revenge. How can a nun be like this in the world? Slanderous words were used to harm me. I suffered all kinds of hardships and grievances. The aunt's anger did not subside but worsened. She caused me to be alone in the temple, suffering bullying. The evil nun plotted to seduce me. I vowed to protect my chastity and refused to comply. My good husband knew nothing and went away to take the exam. My heart was filled with sorrow; to whom could I tell my story? Although my husband has returned and we have had the good fortune to meet, I am even more saddened. The lotus and the barbs have already been formed. Alas, how can I bear to read the poem of heartbrokenness? Alas, teardrops stain my silk handkerchief. Alas, thoughts come to mind, and it is difficult to fall asleep. Alas, I toss and turn all night, unable to sleep. Alas, my haggard appearance is afraid to face the mirror. Alas, I am truly ill on my silk quilt. Alas, the zither should continue the lingering sound of our love. Alas, just as I am about to die, my mother-in-law calls. I cannot serve and care for her morning and evening. I wish to express my sorrow for now. Please forgive your unfilial daughter-in-law. This karma was destined in a previous life. Why blame others for the torment? I only hope that heaven knows my intentions. In this life, drifting like duckweed. I am willing to close my eyes and be in darkness in both worlds.

Ying Yunwei's Special Actors 220

Distressed Miss Chen Bo'er

It was such a ghostly forest, a gloomy and decaying temple, so desolate that even the presiding monk had long disappeared. Hidden inside were a group of revolutionaries, a group of young men and women living under the initial warlord rule. These were Yuan Muzhi, Chen Bo'er, Li Qing, Ying Yin, Yao Ping, Qian Qianli, Sun Jing, Tian Chen, etc. in "With One Heart."

Director Ying Yunwei, in order to increase the chilling atmosphere of the decaying temple, specially hired two special actors. That night, Ying Yunwei said to Chen Bo'er, "The two special actors who will be acting with you are here." Pointing to a jar next to her, she looked at it and said with a frightened expression, "Is that what you talked to me about yesterday?" It turned out that what was placed inside was a wriggling snake and a pair of rats. "The snake will crawl by your side, and the rats will step on your feet," Ying Yunshu continued, startling Chen Bo'er to scream.

Immediately, under the teasing of the director and the workers, the snake was given a rehearsal, climbing on the body of the Jade Emperor statue. Suddenly, the person holding the snake let go, and the snake flew down from the air, startling all the staff and visitors present.

"Motherly Love" Special Issue to be Published 221

The Minsheng Company's first sound film "Motherly Love" special issue will be published soon. The pictorial section features the personal photos and stills of the lead actors Lin Chuchu, Li Keng, Ge Zuozi, Hu Yixing, Zhao Hua, Song Xiaoxie, Gong Zhihua, Fei Boqing, Hong Jingling, Huang Yunzhen, and Wen Rong, as well as photos of the staff and the work situation, occupying a total of twelve full pages with the two-color cover and back cover. The text section includes director Jin Qingyu's director's remarks, and the division of scenes from the film. Among them, the two articles "Funny Stories and Anecdotes" and "Work Diary" collect all the jokes. The Suzhou location shooting notes also have extremely interesting descriptions, as well as the story, the list of actors, miscellaneous writings about the actors, an article written by Ms. Lin Chuchu, signatures of the staff, and the lyrics of the carpenter song sung by Li Keng, occupying a total of twenty pages. The entire book is thirty-two pages thick, and each copy is sold for only five cents.
